<p>Less than a third of those aboard <i>Titanic</i> survived the disaster. Some survivors died shortly afterwards; injuries and the effects of exposure caused the deaths of several of those brought aboard <i>Carpathia</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatonHaas1994179_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatonHaas1994179-230"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> Of the groups shown in the table, 49% of the children, 26% of the female passengers, 82% of the male passengers and 78% of the crew died. The figures show stark differences in the survival rates of the different classes aboard <i>Titanic</i>. Although only 3 percent of first-class women were lost, 54% of those in third class died. Similarly, five of six first-class and all second-class children survived, but 52 of the 79 in third class perished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHowells199994_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHowells199994-231"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> The only first-class child to perish was <a href="/wiki/Allison_family" title="Allison family">Loraine Allison</a>, aged 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> Proportionately, the heaviest losses were suffered by the second-class men, of whom 92% died. Additionally, among the <a href="/wiki/Animals_aboard_the_RMS_Titanic" title="Animals aboard the RMS Titanic">pets brought aboard</a> three survived the sinking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorgiou200018_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorgiou200018-233"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinking_of_the_RMS_Titanic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-shiptime-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-shiptime_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-shiptime_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">At the time of the collision, <i>Titanic</i> '​s clocks were set to 2 hours 2 minutes ahead of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">Eastern Time Zone</a> and 2 hours 58 minutes behind <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Mean_Time" title="Greenwich Mean Time">Greenwich Mean Time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalpern201178_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalpern201178-2"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The 3rd was to be the RMS <i>Britannic</i> which never saw service as a liner; instead she was requisitioned directly into service as His Majesty's Hospital Ship <a href="/wiki/HMHS_Britannic" title="HMHS Britannic">(HMHS) <i>Britannic</i></a> (during WWI).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-wireless-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-wireless_22-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Radio telegraphy was known as <a href="/wiki/Wireless_telegraphy" title="Wireless telegraphy">"wireless"</a> in the British English of the period.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-growler-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-growler_24-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-growler_24-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><img alt="" data-file-height="1089" data-file-width="1000" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Wiktionary-logo-en.svg/15px-Wiktionary-logo-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Wiktionary-logo-en.svg/22px-Wiktionary-logo-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Wiktionary-logo-en.svg/29px-Wiktionary-logo-en.svg.png 2x" width="15"/> The dictionary definition of <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/growler" title="wiktionary:growler">growler</a> at Wiktionary:  "A small iceberg or ice floe which is barely visible over the surface of the water."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Despite later myth, featured for example in the <a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">1997 film <i>Titanic</i></a>, the ship <i>Titanic</i> was not attempting to set a transatlantic speed record; the White Star Line had made a conscious decision not to compete with their rivals <a href="/wiki/Cunard_Line" title="Cunard Line">Cunard</a> on speed, but instead to focus on size and luxury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBartlett201124_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBartlett201124-29"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-87">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">An incident confirmed this philosophy while <i>Titanic</i> was under construction: the White Star liner <i>Republic</i> was involved in a collision and sank. Even though she did not have enough lifeboats for all passengers, they were all saved because the ship was able to stay afloat long enough for them to be ferried to ships coming to assist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChirnside200429_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChirnside200429-86"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
